###begin article-title 0
###xml 58 62 58 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 74 79 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Loss of ALS2/Alsin Exacerbates Motor Dysfunction in a SOD1H46R-Expressing Mouse ALS Model by Disturbing Endolysosomal Trafficking
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: SH AO JEI. Performed the experiments: SH AO RK KSU AA MK. Analyzed the data: SH AO AA MK YU. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: SH AO AA MK MA YU YI JEI. Wrote the paper: SH AO RK KSU JEI.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Background
###end title 2
###begin p 3
ALS2/alsin is a guanine nucleotide exchange factor for the small GTPase Rab5 and involved in macropinocytosis-associated endosome fusion and trafficking, and neurite outgrowth. ALS2 deficiency accounts for a number of juvenile recessive motor neuron diseases (MNDs). Recently, it has been shown that ALS2 plays a role in neuroprotection against MND-associated pathological insults, such as toxicity induced by mutant Cu/Zn superoxide dismutase (SOD1). However, molecular mechanisms underlying the relationship between ALS2-associated cellular function and its neuroprotective role remain unclear.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Methodology/Principal Findings
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 173 177 173 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 185 189 185 189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 181 189 181 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 203 207 203 207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 199 207 199 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 572 576 572 576 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 568 576 568 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 850 854 850 854 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 846 854 846 854 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 134 138 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 209 224 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">transgenic mice</span>
###xml 577 581 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 855 859 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To address this issue, we investigated the molecular and pathological basis for the phenotypic modification of mutant SOD1-expressing mice by ALS2 loss. Genetic ablation of Als2 in SOD1H46R, but not SOD1G93A, transgenic mice aggravated the mutant SOD1-associated disease symptoms such as body weight loss and motor dysfunction, leading to the earlier death. Light and electron microscopic examinations revealed the presence of degenerating and/or swollen spinal axons accumulating granular aggregates and autophagosome-like vesicles in early- and even pre-symptomatic SOD1H46R mice. Further, enhanced accumulation of insoluble high molecular weight SOD1, poly-ubiquitinated proteins, and macroautophagy-associated proteins such as polyubiquitin-binding protein p62/SQSTM1 and a lipidated form of light chain 3 (LC3-II), emerged in ALS2-deficient SOD1H46R mice. Intriguingly, ALS2 was colocalized with LC3 and p62, and partly with SOD1 on autophagosome/endosome hybrid compartments, and loss of ALS2 significantly lowered the lysosome-dependent clearance of LC3 and p62 in cultured cells.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Conclusions/Significance
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 245 249 245 249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 544 551 544 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Based on these observations, although molecular basis for the distinctive susceptibilities to ALS2 loss in different mutant SOD1-expressing ALS models is still elusive, disturbance of the endolysosomal system by ALS2 loss may exacerbate the SOD1H46R-mediated neurotoxicity by accelerating the accumulation of immature vesicles and misfolded proteins in the spinal cord. We propose that ALS2 is implicated in endolysosomal trafficking through the fusion between endosomes and autophagosomes, thereby regulating endolysosomal protein degradation in vivo.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
Introduction
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 253 256 253 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Pasinelli1">[1]</xref>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALS2</italic>
###xml 446 450 446 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SETX</italic>
###xml 459 468 459 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SPATACSIN</italic>
###xml 469 474 469 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SPG11</italic>
###xml 483 486 483 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FUS</italic>
###xml 495 499 495 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">VAPB</italic>
###xml 508 511 508 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ANG</italic>
###xml 524 530 524 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TARDBP</italic>
###xml 578 581 578 581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Pasinelli1">[1]</xref>
###xml 583 586 583 586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Dion1">[2]</xref>
###xml 588 591 588 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Orlacchio1">[3]</xref>
Amyotrophic lateral sclerosis (ALS) is a heterogeneous group of progressive neurodegenerative disorders characterized by a selective loss of upper motor neurons (UMN) in the cerebral cortex and lower motor neurons (LMN) in the brainstem and spinal cord [1]. While most of the cases reported are sporadic, 5-10% are familial. Thus far, more than 10 ALS-associated loci have been assigned, and several causative genes, including SOD1 (ALS1), ALS2, SETX (ALS4), SPATACSIN/SPG11 (ALS5), FUS (ALS6), VAPB (ALS8), ANG (ALS9), and TARDBP (ALS10) have been identified and characterized [1], [2], [3].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALS2</italic>
###xml 97 100 97 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano1">[4]</xref>
###xml 102 105 102 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Yang1">[5]</xref>
###xml 107 110 107 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano2">[6]</xref>
###xml 161 164 161 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-BenHamida1">[7]</xref>
###xml 222 225 222 225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-LermanSagie1">[8]</xref>
###xml 308 311 308 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-EymardPierre1">[9]</xref>
###xml 453 457 453 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALS2</italic>
###xml 504 507 504 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano1">[4]</xref>
###xml 509 512 509 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Yang1">[5]</xref>
###xml 514 517 514 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano2">[6]</xref>
###xml 519 523 519 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Sztriha1">[10]</xref>
###xml 525 529 525 529 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-VerschuurenBemelmans1">[11]</xref>
###xml 531 535 531 535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Herzfeld1">[12]</xref>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Mintchev1">[13]</xref>
###xml 543 547 543 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Shirakawa1">[14]</xref>
###xml 691 695 691 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALS2</italic>
###xml 830 834 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Otomo1">[15]</xref>
###xml 911 915 911 915 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Kunita1">[16]</xref>
###xml 917 921 917 921 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Otomo2">[17]</xref>
###xml 945 949 945 949 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Otomo2">[17]</xref>
###xml 951 955 951 955 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Jacquier1">[18]</xref>
###xml 957 961 957 961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Jacquier2">[19]</xref>
###xml 1049 1053 1049 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALS2</italic>
###xml 1359 1362 1359 1362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano2">[6]</xref>
###xml 1364 1368 1364 1368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano3">[20]</xref>
###xml 1370 1374 1370 1374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Cai1">[21]</xref>
###xml 1086 1091 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1197 1201 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
ALS2 is a causative gene for a juvenile autosomal recessive form of motor neuron diseases (MNDs) [4], [5], [6], including amyotrophic lateral sclerosis 2 (ALS2) [7] (OMIM 205100), juvenile primary lateral sclerosis (PLSJ) [8] (OMIM 606353), and infantile-onset ascending hereditary spastic paralysis (IAHSP) [9] (OMIM 607225). These disorders are characterized by ascending degeneration of UMN with or without LMN involvement. A total of 19 independent ALS2 mutations from 17 families have been reported [4], [5], [6], [10], [11], [12], [13], [14]. They are predicted to result in either premature termination of translation or substitution of an evolutionarily conserved amino acid for the ALS2-coded protein, ALS2 or alsin, leading to loss of its function. ALS2 is a guanine nucleotide exchange factor for the small GTPase Rab5 [15] and involves in macropinocytosis-associated endosome trafficking and fusion [16], [17], and neurite outgrowth [17], [18], [19]. Loss of these functions accounts for motor dysfunction and axonal degeneration in the ALS2-linked MNDs. Logically designed mouse studies could provide persuasive evidence that loss of ALS2 triggers motor neuron degeneration. However, mice lacking ALS2 cannot recapitulate the complex disease phenotypes, despite the subclinical levels of motor dysfunction and axonal degeneration in aged animals [6], [20], [21]. Thus, although there are potentially important clinical implications of these observations, the physiological functions of ALS2 and the molecular mechanisms underlying the motor dysfunction resulting from ALS2 deficiency remain to be clarified.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 82 86 82 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1</italic>
###xml 210 214 210 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Rosen1">[22]</xref>
###xml 240 244 240 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1</italic>
###xml 406 410 406 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Kato1">[23]</xref>
###xml 816 819 816 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Pasinelli1">[1]</xref>
###xml 821 825 821 825 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Boillee1">[24]</xref>
###xml 303 308 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Most efforts to delineate ALS/MND pathogenesis have converged on the mutations in SOD1, encoding Cu/Zn superoxide dismutase (SOD1), which accounts for most prevalent form of the autosomal dominant familial ALS [22]. More than 120 different SOD1 mutations have been identified (), and several transgenic mouse lines expressing disease causative SOD1 mutants have been generated and thoroughly characterized [23]. Nonetheless, no consensus has yet emerged as to how SOD1 mutations lead to selective death of motor neurons, except that multiple toxicity pathways including oxidative stress, endoplasmic reticulum (ER) stress, excitotoxicity, mitochondrial dysfunction, neural inflammation, protein misfolding and accumulation, and dysfunctional intracellular trafficking, are implicated in the pathogenesis of ALS/MNDs [1], [24].
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 135 139 135 139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Kanekura1">[25]</xref>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Lai1">[26]</xref>
###xml 276 277 276 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 352 356 352 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Panzeri1">[27]</xref>
###xml 368 372 368 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Cai2">[28]</xref>
###xml 561 568 561 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 679 683 679 683 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 675 683 675 683 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 689 693 689 693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Lin1">[29]</xref>
###xml 695 699 695 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Deng1">[30]</xref>
###xml 798 805 798 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1029 1033 1029 1033 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 1025 1033 1025 1033 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 1098 1102 1098 1102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Lin1">[29]</xref>
###xml 378 382 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 684 688 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1034 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Recently, it has been reported that overexpression of ALS2 protects cultured motor neuronal cells from toxicity induced by mutant SOD1 [25]. Further, loss of ALS2 renders neurons more susceptible to excitotoxicity [26], while cell death induced by neurotoxic stimuli, such as N-methyl-D-aspartate, is significantly suppressed by overexpression of ALS2 [27]. Moreover, Als2-null mice are slightly vulnerable to oxidative stress [28]. These observations imply a neuroprotective function of ALS2 against ALS/MND-associated pathological insults. On the other hand, in vivo studies have demonstrated that loss of ALS2 does not affect the motor neuron degeneration and survival of SOD1G93A mice [29], [30], which does not support the functional interaction between ALS2 and mutant SOD1-mediated toxicity in vivo. However, with the use of only a single mutant SOD1 transgenic line, such notions still remain inconclusive. Rather, it is possible that the extremely rapid progression of motor dysfunction observed in high-copy number SOD1G93A mice could overwhelm the modest symptoms by the ALS2 deficiency [29].
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 37 41 37 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 33 41 33 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 164 168 164 168 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Sasaki1">[31]</xref>
###xml 184 188 184 188 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 180 188 180 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 213 217 213 217 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 209 217 209 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 255 259 255 259 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 251 259 251 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 361 365 361 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Aoki1">[32]</xref>
###xml 422 426 422 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 703 710 703 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 42 46 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 189 193 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 218 222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 458 462 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To clarify these issues, we used SOD1H46R mice, which exhibit a widespread axonal degeneration with slowly progressive motor neuron degeneration in the spinal cord [31] instead of SOD1G93A mice, and generated SOD1H46R mice on an Als2-null background. SOD1H46R mutation accounts for a mild form of familial ALS that was originally identified in Japanese kindred [32]. We here revealed that loss of ALS2 exacerbated the SOD1H46R-associated disease symptoms in mice, and identified ALS2 as a novel regulator for the endolysosomal system. Our findings suggest that ALS2 plays a role in the maturation of autophagosomes through the endosome-autophagosome fusion, thereby regulating endolysosomal trafficking in vivo.
###end p 13
###begin title 14
Results
###end title 14
###begin title 15
###xml 50 54 50 54 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 46 54 46 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 55 59 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Loss of ALS2 results in a shorter lifespan in SOD1H46R mice
###end title 15
###begin p 16

###xml 206 209 206 209 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 210 218 210 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 220 224 220 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 224 227 224 227 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 232 236 232 236 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 228 236 228 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 242 246 242 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 246 249 246 249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 254 258 254 258 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 250 258 250 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 329 337 329 337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s013">Table S1</xref>
###xml 365 369 365 369 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 361 369 361 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 405 409 393 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Sasaki1">[31]</xref>
###xml 447 451 435 439 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Alexander1">[33]</xref>
###xml 511 520 499 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s001">Figure S1</xref>
To investigate the effect of ALS2 expression on the pathogenesis for mutant SOD1-mediated MNDs, we generated congenic lines (C57BL/6N) with 6 different genotypes; Als2+/+ (wild-type), Als2+/-, Als2-/-, Als2+/+;SOD1H46R, Als2+/-;SOD1H46R, and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R. The mutant alleles were transmitted in the expected Mendelian ratio (Table S1). A copy number of the SOD1H46R transgene (approximately20 copies) [31], which affected the disease severity [33], remained unchanged in the course of these mating schemes (Figure S1).
###end p 16

###xml 962 971 962 971 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g001">Figure 1D</xref>
###xml 976 978 976 978 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s003">S3</xref>
###xml 1068 1072 1068 1072 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 1126 1130 1126 1130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 1122 1130 1122 1130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 1167 1177 1167 1177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
###xml 1202 1206 1202 1206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Lin1">[29]</xref>
###xml 1208 1212 1208 1212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Deng1">[30]</xref>
###xml 1255 1259 1255 1259 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 1282 1289 1282 1289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 60 64 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 141 145 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 345 349 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 586 590 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 764 779 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">transgenic mice</span>
###xml 791 796 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 847 851 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 956 960 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1087 1091 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1131 1135 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
During the experimental periods, both wild-type and Als2-/- mice showed a constant increase in their body weight (Figure S2A and S2B), while mice carrying the SOD1H46R transgene reached their maximum body weight at 12-14 weeks of age, and terminally decreased as disease symptoms progressed (Figure 1A and 1B). Notably, loss of ALS2 in SOD1H46R mice (Als2-/-;SOD1H46R) showed a marked and earlier decrease in their body weight compared to either Als2+/+;SOD1H46R or Als2+/-;SOD1H46R littermates (Figure 1A and 1B). Further, Kaplan-Meier survival analysis revealed that Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice died earlier than either Als2+/+;SOD1H46R or Als2+/-;SOD1H46R littermates (Figure 1C). Importantly, these exacerbated phenotypes by ALS2 loss were restorable by crossing to transgenic mice expressing human ALS2 (ALS2-tg; line L34-1) (Als2-/-;SOD1H46R;ALS2 mice), albeit ALS2 overexpression per se did not show any obvious beneficial effects on lifespan in SOD1H46R mice (Figure 1D and S3). The results indicate that loss of ALS2 aggravates disease symptoms associated with SOD1H46R expression in mice. By contrast, loss of ALS2 in SOD1G93A mice did not affect their lifespan (Figure S2C) as previously reported [29], [30], suggesting a limited role of ALS2 in SOD1G93A-mediated pathogenesis in vivo.
###end p 17

Loss of ALS2 results in accelerated body weight loss with shorter lifespan in SOD1H46R mice.

###xml 469 472 469 472 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>

(A) Growth curves for female mice [wild-type (WT) (black circle; n = 14-33), Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (blue square; n = 6-30), Als2+/-;SOD1H46R (green triangle; n = 28-84), and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R (red inverted triangle; n = 7-44)], and (B) for male mice [WT (n = 41-48), Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (n = 14-46), Als2+/-;SOD1H46R (n = 9-76), and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R (n = 8-36)]. (A-B) In either gender, age at which body weight loss began in Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice was earlier than that for Als2+/+;SOD1H46R mice (female; ***p<0.001, at 22 weeks, male; ***p<0.001 and **p<0.01, at 21 and 22 weeks respectively). There were no differences in the mean values between Als2+/+;SOD1H46R and Als2+/-;SOD1H46R mice at any ages. The values for SOD1H46R-expressing mice (Als2+/+;SOD1H46R, Als2+/-;SOD1H46R, and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R) later than 8 weeks of ages were all significantly lower than those for WT animals (levels of significance were not shown). Values are mean+/-SD. Statistical significance is evaluated by ANOVA with Tukey's post hoc test. (C) Survival curves for WT [black; n = 55 (female; n = 14, male; n = 41)], Als2-/- [orange; n = 78 (female; n = 32, male; n = 46)], Als2+/+;SOD1H46R [blue circle; n = 48 (female; n = 13, male; n = 35)], Als2+/-;SOD1H46R [green square; n = 132 (female; n = 63, male; n = 69)], and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R [red triangle; n = 57 (female; n = 27, male; n = 30)]. Kaplan-Meier analysis identified significant difference between Als2-/-;SOD1H46R and Als2+/+;SOD1H46R, and between Als2-/-;SOD1H46R and Als2+/-;SOD1H46R (Log-rank test; p<0.0001). (D) Survival curves for Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (blue circle; same as C), Als2+/+;SOD1H46R;ALS2 [gray square; n = 25 (female; n = 13, male; n = 12)], and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R;ALS2 [pink triangle; n = 11 (female; n = 4, male; n = 7)]. Kaplan-Meier analysis identified no significant differences between groups.

###begin p 21
###xml 23 27 23 27 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 160 164 160 164 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>

###xml 605 609 581 585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 609 612 585 588 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 617 621 593 597 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 613 621 589 597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 625 629 601 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 629 632 605 608 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 637 641 613 617 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 633 641 609 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 655 664 631 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 872 876 848 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 876 879 852 855 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 884 888 860 864 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 880 888 856 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 968 972 944 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 972 975 948 951 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 980 984 956 960 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 976 984 952 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 1047 1063 1023 1039 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g002">Figure 2B and 2C</xref>
###xml 3 7 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 165 169 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 423 427 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 823 827 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 889 893 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
As mice expressing SOD1H46R exhibited progressive motor dysfunction and paralysis, particularly of the hind limbs, we next assessed whether loss of ALS2 in SOD1H46R mice affects the course of motor deficits by conducting quantitative behavioral analyses. First, to evaluate motor coordination and balance, we performed balance beam test, by which the onset of disease could be sensitively determined [34]. Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice showed an earlier motor dysfunction, in which the onset of disease (approximately15 weeks of age) was approximately 3 weeks earlier than those (approximately18 weeks of age) of Als2+/+;SOD1H46R or Als2+/-;SOD1H46R littermates (Figure 2A). Further, analyses of rearing and cage activities revealed that although there were no significant differences in their activities among all pre-symptomatic mice (12 weeks of age) with different genotypes, Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice showed a significantly lower spontaneous motor activity than wild-type or Als2+/-;SOD1H46R littermates at a later stage of the disease (18 week of age) (Figure 2B and 2C).
###end p 21

###xml 49 53 49 53 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 45 53 45 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 54 58 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Loss of ALS2 aggravates motor dysfunction in SOD1H46R mice.
###end title 22

(A) Changes in the balance beam test scores in wild-type (WT) (black circle), Als2-/- (orange square), Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (blue triangle), Als2+/-;SOD1H46R (green inverted triangle), and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R (red diamond) mice. Values are means+/-SEM [each genotype; n = 20 (female; n = 10, male; n = 10)]. Statistical significance is evaluated by ANOVA with Scheffe's post hoc test. There are significant differences between Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (blue) and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R (red) mice (*p<0.05, **p<0.01, or ***p<0.001 at 15-21 weeks of ages), and between Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (blue) and Als2+/-;SOD1H46R (green) mice (++p<0.01 at 21 weeks of age). (B) The rearing and (C) cage activities in wild-type (Als2+/+), Als2+/-;SOD1H46R, and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice in a dark (gray) and a light (white) cycle at 12 and 18 weeks of ages. Cumulative data counting for 7 consecutive days are shown as Box-Wisker plots [AU; arbitrary unit, each genotype; n = 8-10 (female)]. Statistical significance is evaluated by non-parametric ANOVA (Kruskal-Wallis) with Dunn's post hoc test. There are significant differences in the rearing activities (dark & light) between wild-type (Als2+/+) and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (***p<0.01), in the rearing activities (light) between Als2+/-;SOD1H46R and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (***p<0.05), and in the cage activities between wild-type (Als2+/+) and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (***p<0.01) at 18 weeks of age.

###begin title 24
###xml 4 8 4 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 9 13 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
SOD1H46R mice show an axonal degeneration in the spinal tracts from an early symptomatic stage
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 370 374 370 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 374 377 374 377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 382 386 382 386 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 378 386 378 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 393 402 393 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 150 154 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 387 391 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To determine whether these motor phenotypes are associated with motor neuron degeneration, we conducted histological analyses using early symptomatic mice (16-18 weeks of age). Although there were no evidences for the motor neuron loss at this stage, a wide-spread axonal degeneration in the spinal tracts of the lateral and ventral columns was evident, particularly in Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (Figure 3A).
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 4 8 4 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 20 24 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
SOD1H46R-expressing mice show axonal degeneration and swelling in the spinal cord.

(A) Representative toluidine blue staining of the transverse section of lumbar spinal cord (L4-L5) from 18-week-old wild-type (WT; upper row), 16-week-old Als2+/+;SOD1H46R (middle row), and 16-week-old Als2-/-;SOD1H46R (lower row) mice. Images for the dorsal columns, lateral columns, ventral columns, and ventral horn cells were shown. Red arrowheads indicate degenerating axons. Axonal degeneration is most prominent in Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice. Scale bars = 20 microm. (B-F) Representative electron micrographs of lumbar (L4-L5) spinal axons from Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mouse at 16 weeks (B-F) and 8 weeks (G). Degenerating axon (B), axon accumulating fibrillar materials and multivesicular bodies (C and c'), membrane saccule containing granular/osmiophilic aggregates and autophagosome-like vesicles (D and d', red arrowhead), axon containing osmiophilic and autophagosome-like (red arrowhead) vesicles (E and e'), astrocyte containing osmiophilic aggregates (F), and swollen axon accumulating granular aggregates and vesicles (G), are shown. Scale bars are as indicated.

###xml 420 428 420 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 433 437 433 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 437 440 437 440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 441 449 441 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 486 502 486 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3B and 3C</xref>
###xml 576 585 576 585 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3D</xref>
###xml 620 629 620 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3E</xref>
###xml 725 734 725 734 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3F</xref>
###xml 749 753 749 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 753 756 753 756 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 761 765 761 765 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 757 765 757 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 855 864 855 864 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g003">Figure 3G</xref>
###xml 894 898 894 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 898 901 898 901 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 906 910 906 910 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 902 910 902 910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 1098 1102 1098 1102 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 450 454 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 766 770 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 911 915 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1114 1118 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To investigate the histopathology in more detail, we next conducted an electron microscopic (EM) analysis. Although there were no observable abnormalities in soma of motor neurons (data not shown), we observed the degenerative and swollen axons with the accumulation of granular aggregates, disorganized fibrillar materials, multivesicular bodies (MVBs), and/or autophagosome-like vesicles in the spinal cord of Als2-/-;SOD1H46R and Als2+/+;SOD1H46R mice at an early symptomatic stage (Figure 3B and 3C). Further, membrane saccules containing granular/osmiophilic aggregates (Figure 3D) and autophagosome-like vesicles (Figure 3E) were observed. Astrocytes containing osmiophillic aggregates were also occasionally observed (Figure 3F). Notably, in Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice, these pathologic phenotypes were evident even at 8 weeks of pre-symptomatic stage (Figure 3G), but not in a same stage of Als2+/+;SOD1H46R mice (data not shown). These data underscore the relevance of axonal dysfunction and/or degeneration, probably caused by the dysfunctional axonal trafficking, on the disease onset in SOD1H46R-expressing mice.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 99 103 99 103 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 95 103 95 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>

Loss of ALS2 promotes the progressive accumulation of insoluble proteins in the spinal cord of SOD1H46R mice

###xml 312 316 312 316 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>

###xml 396 400 396 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 392 400 392 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 472 476 472 476 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 214 218 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 232 237 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 401 405 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
First, we confirmed that there were no significant differences in the expression levels of the SOD1H46R transcript (Figure S4A) and soluble SOD1H46R protein (Figure 4, S5A, and S6A) among three different groups of mice carrying the human SOD1 transgene; i.e., Als2+/+;SOD1H46R, Als2+/-;SOD1H46R, and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R. These results indicate that the exacerbation of motor dysfunction seen in SOD1H46R mice lacking ALS2 was not simply due to the increased level of the SOD1H46R expression.
###end p 31

###xml 1333 1341 1333 1341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1343 1351 1343 1351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s005">S5G, S5I</xref>
###xml 1353 1365 1353 1365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s006">S6C, and S6D</xref>
###xml 1494 1503 1494 1503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1594 1597 1594 1597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vim</italic>

###xml 1697 1705 1697 1705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 1707 1713 1707 1713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sqstm1</italic>
###xml 1725 1733 1725 1733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Map1lc3a</italic>
###xml 1734 1742 1734 1742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Map1lc3b</italic>
###xml 1769 1778 1769 1778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 2045 2049 2045 2049 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Kabuta1">[37]</xref>
###xml 2051 2055 2051 2055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Gal1">[38]</xref>
###xml 2218 2222 2218 2222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 2214 2222 2214 2222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 126 130 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 628 632 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1327 1331 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2223 2227 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To identify the molecular factors that were associated with behavioral and pathological features observed in Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice, we conducted western blot analysis of the lumbo-sacral cord extracts using a panel of antibodies, and performed their quantitative analyses. Although the levels of the ALS-related neuronal intermediate filament proteins [peripherin and neurofilament heavy chain (NFH)] [35] and the ALS-causative gene product [TAR DNA-binding protein 43-kD (TDP-43)] [1], [2] were unchanged, a progressive accumulation of insoluble high-molecular weight (HMW) SOD1 and poly-ubiquitinated proteins was observed in mice expressing SOD1H46R, particularly in those lacking ALS2 (Als2-/-;SOD1H46R) (Figure 4, S5B, S5C, S5E, S6A, and S6B). Further, from 16 weeks of pre- and early-symptomatic stage, glial intermediate filament proteins, vimentin and glial fibrillary acidic protein (GFAP), were accumulated (Figure 4, S5J, S5K, and S6E). Remarkably, the levels of two macroautophagy (hereafter referred to as autophagy)-associated proteins, polyubiquitin binding protein p62/SQSTM1 (p62) and a lipidated-form of microtubule-associated protein 1-light chain 3 (LC3-II), both of which were selectively degraded by autophagy-lysosomal system [36], were significantly increased in insoluble fractions of Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (Figure 4, S5G, S5I, S6C, and S6D). Similar results were obtained in samples from the brainstem, cerebellum, and cervical cord, but not from the cerebral cortex (Figure S7). A quantitative reverse transcriptase PCR (qRT-PCR) revealed that although expression of Vim and Gfap was significantly upregulated as the disease progressed, no transcriptional activation of SOD1H46R, Sqstm1 (p62), and Map1lc3a/Map1lc3b (LC3A/LC3B) was observed (Figure S4). These results suggest that the accumulation of insoluble mutant SOD1, p62, and LC3-II is not simply due to an increased expression of these proteins, but rather to a decrease in their degradation. Since mutant SOD1 is degraded by both the proteasome and autophagy [37], [38], impairment of the ubiquitin-proteasome system (UPS) and/or the autophagy-endolysosomal system could result in the accumulation of such insoluble proteins in SOD1H46R mice, particularly in those lacking ALS2.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
Proteasome activity in the spinal cord is increased as the disease progresses
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 280 284 280 284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 355 363 355 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 451 455 451 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 455 458 455 458 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 503 507 503 507 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 499 507 499 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 617 625 617 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 787 791 787 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 791 794 791 794 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 799 803 799 803 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 795 803 795 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 810 818 810 818 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 853 857 853 857 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Cheroni1">[39]</xref>
###xml 859 863 859 863 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Puttaparthi1">[40]</xref>
###xml 1002 1010 998 1006 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1054 1058 1050 1054 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 1050 1058 1046 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 1329 1333 1325 1329 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 1325 1333 1321 1329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 170 174 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 296 300 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 508 512 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 804 808 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1059 1063 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1334 1338 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To investigate the contribution of UPS impairment on the protein accumulation observed, we analyzed the catalytic activity for the 20S proteasome in the spinal cord from mice with different genotypes. Surprisingly, the proteasomal activity was induced rather than impaired in SOD1H46R-expressing mice at a late symptomatic stage (20 and 23 weeks of age) (Figure 5). Although loss of ALS2 by itself did not affect the proteasome activity (wild-type vs Als2-/- at 18 weeks of age), ALS2 deficiency in SOD1H46R mice seems to result in the earlier enhancement of proteasome activity in the spinal cord (20 weeks of age) (Figure 5), which might be correlated with the disease progression. Importantly, the levels of LMP2, a inducible subunit of immunoproteasome, was increased in symptomatic Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice (Figure 4), consistent with recent findings [39], [40]. Since the levels of the constitutive subunits of 20S proteasome (alpha5 and C2) and one of the molecular chaperone Hsp70 were unchanged (Figure 4), the UPS was not severely affected in SOD1H46R mice, at least, at the disease stages examined, but rather enhanced in certain cell types within the spinal cord in response to the disease progression. Thus, the accelerated accumulation of HMW SOD1 and polyubiquitinated proteins from an early symptomatic stage in SOD1H46R mice is not simply due to impairment of the UPS.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 46 50 46 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 42 50 42 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 51 55 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Proteasome activity in the spinal cord of SOD1H46R mice is increased as the disease progresses.
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 132 136 132 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>

###xml 145 148 145 148 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>

###xml 163 167 163 167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>

###xml 347 355 345 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">post hoc</italic>

###xml 81 85 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>

Values are mean +/- SD (n = 3-5) in percent (%) relative to 18 week-old wild-type mice. Statistical significance is evaluated by ANOVA with Bonferroni's post hoc test (*p<0.05, ***p<0.001).
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 4 8 4 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 9 13 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
SOD1H46R mice reveal the accumulation of ubiquitin, p62, and LC3 in the spinal cord
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 165 169 165 169 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 269 279 269 279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s008">Figure S8A</xref>
###xml 315 319 315 319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 311 319 311 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>G93A</sup></italic>
###xml 325 329 325 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Bruijn1">[41]</xref>
###xml 436 446 436 446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s008">Figure S8B</xref>
###xml 485 489 485 489 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 619 623 619 623 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G93A</sup>
###xml 623 627 623 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Strom1">[42]</xref>
###xml 673 681 673 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 721 725 721 725 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 145 149 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 320 324 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 430 434 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To investigate the cellular localization of the accumulated insoluble proteins in the spinal cord, we performed immunohistochemical analysis. In mice expressing SOD1H46R, a higher SOD1-immunoreactivity was observed throughout white and gray matters of the spinal cord (Figure S8A). However, unlike in a case of SOD1G93A mice [41], no obvious SOD1-positive inclusions were detected, at least, in the samples from early symptomatic mice (Figure S8B), consistent with the notion that SOD1H46R shows minimal tendency to form the aggregates or inclusions when compared with other aggregation-prone SOD1 mutants, such as SOD1G93A[42]. HMW insoluble SOD1 observed in immunoblots (Figure 4) may represent oligomeric forms of SOD1H46R that are not analogous to the aggregates of other SOD1 mutants, and are thus invisible under the light-microscopic observations.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 224 228 224 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 228 231 228 231 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 236 240 236 240 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 232 240 232 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 245 249 245 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 249 252 249 252 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 257 261 257 261 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 253 261 253 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 290 299 290 299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 323 327 323 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 327 330 327 330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 335 339 335 339 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 331 339 331 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 346 350 346 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 350 353 350 353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 358 362 358 362 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 354 362 354 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 523 532 523 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 818 826 818 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 1058 1067 1058 1067 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 1330 1334 1330 1334 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Komatsu1">[36]</xref>
###xml 1473 1477 1473 1477 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 218 222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 340 344 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 363 367 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1509 1513 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Expression of p62 was evident in microtubule-associated protein 2 (MAP2)-positive large motor neurons but not in GFAP-positive astrocytes in the spinal cord, and the levels of p62 were higher in mutant SOD1-expressing mice (Als2+/+;SOD1H46R and Als2-/-;SOD1H46R) than in wild-type control (Figure 6A). Further, compared to Als2+/+;SOD1H46R mice, Als2-/-;SOD1H46R mice showed more intense p62-immunoreactivities in both large and smaller-sized neurons, and the formation of large p62-positive aggregates was more prominent (Figure 6A). Co-immunostaining of p62 with a number of cellular markers revealed that although the p62-positive large aggregates were occasionally colocalized with MAP2, they were mostly surrounded by astrocytes, but not colocalized with astrocyte, myelin, oligodendrocyte, or microglia markers (Figure 6 and data not shown). These results suggest that the large aggregates are present in extracellular spaces. Importantly, triple-immunostaning demonstrated that these large aggregates simultaneously contained p62, ubiquitin, and LC3 (Figure 6B). Thus, it is possible that these ubiquitin/p62/LC3-positive aggregates in the extracellular space are derived from the degenerated dendrites and/or axons. Since the accumulated polyubiquitinated proteins, p62, and LC3-II are a hallmark of the autophagic defect [36], we hypothesize that loss of ALS2 associates with deregulation of the endolysosomal bulk protein degradation, thereby aggravating the SOD1H46R-associated disease symptoms in mice.
###end p 41
###begin title 42
###xml 4 8 4 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 20 24 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
SOD1H46R-expressing mice show the accumulation of ubiquitin, p62, and LC3 in the spinal cord.
###end title 42

###xml 500 504 496 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 504 507 500 503 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 512 516 508 512 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 508 516 504 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 523 524 519 520 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</bold>
###xml 538 542 534 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 542 545 538 541 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>

###xml 763 764 755 756 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 968 972 960 964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 972 975 964 967 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 980 984 972 976 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 976 984 968 976 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 1015 1019 1007 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1019 1022 1011 1014 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1027 1031 1019 1023 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H46R</sup>
###xml 1023 1031 1015 1023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOD1<sup>H46R</sup></italic>
###xml 277 281 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>

The p62-single positive aggregates are also observed (white arrowheads). Scale bars = 10 microm.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
ALS2 is colocalized with autophagosomal proteins in cultured cells
###end title 44
###begin p 45
###xml 366 382 366 382 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g007">Figure 7A and 7B</xref>
###xml 465 474 465 474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 489 498 489 498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
###xml 839 848 839 848 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009805.s009">Figure S9</xref>
###xml 1010 1014 1010 1014 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Otomo1">[15]</xref>
###xml 1016 1020 1016 1020 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Kunita1">[16]</xref>
###xml 1129 1133 1129 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Berg1">[43]</xref>
To investigate the physiological role of ALS2 and its relationship with the autophagy-associated endolysosomal system, we performed a colocalization study for ALS2, p62, LC3, and other organelle markers using cultured cells. Distribution of ectopically expressed ALS2 and EGFP-LC3 extensively overlapped with endogenous p62 in vesicular compartments in fibroblasts (Figure 7A and 7B). Further, ectopically expressed ALS2 was colocalized with either endogenous p62 (Figure 7C) or EGFP-LC3 (Figure 7D) onto the vesicular compartments in primary hippocampal neurons. Analysis with organella markers in HeLa cells revealed that ALS2/LC3 double-positive vesicles were partially co-stained with either p62, early endosome antigen 1 (EEA1; early endosome marker), or lysosome-associated membrane protein 2 (LAMP2; late endosome/lysosome marker) (Figure S9), but not with the mitochondrial, ER, and Golgi markers (data not shown). These results indicate that ALS2 is present not only onto endosomes and macropinosomes [15], [16], but also onto autophagosomes and/or autophagosome/endosome hybrid vesicular compartments called amphisomes [43].
###end p 45
###begin title 46
ALS2 is colocalized with LC3 and p62 onto vesicular compartments in cultured cells.
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 1 2 1 2 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>

###xml 578 579 578 579 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 638 639 638 639 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</bold>
###xml 641 642 641 642 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</bold>
###xml 648 649 648 649 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</bold>
###xml 707 708 707 708 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 938 939 938 939 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</bold>

###xml 1214 1215 1214 1215 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</bold>

###end p 47
###begin title 48
Loss of ALS2 results in a decreased level of lysosomal clearance of autophagy-associated proteins in fibroblasts
###end title 48
###begin p 49
###xml 144 148 144 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Hadano3">[20]</xref>
###xml 173 177 173 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Lai2">[44]</xref>
###xml 360 364 360 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 364 367 364 367 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 416 420 416 420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Rubinsztein1">[45]</xref>
###xml 723 727 723 727 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009805-Rubinsztein1">[45]</xref>
###xml 928 932 928 932 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 932 935 932 935 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 967 976 967 976 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g008">Figure 8A</xref>
###xml 1134 1138 1134 1138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1138 1141 1138 1141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1291 1300 1291 1300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g008">Figure 8A</xref>
###xml 1364 1368 1364 1368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1368 1371 1368 1371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1435 1444 1435 1444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009805-g008">Figure 8A</xref>
###xml 368 372 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Previously, it has been shown that ALS2 regulates the trafficking and clearance of internalized molecules such as epidermal growth factor (EGF) [20] and glutamate receptors [44] in cultured cells. To further clarify the functional interaction of ALS2 with the autophagosomal-endolysosomal protein degradation in general, fibroblasts derived from wild-type and Als2-/- mice were subjected to autophagic-flux analysis [45]. Since the intracellular levels of LC3-II correlate with the number of autophagosomes, which is regulated by a balance between autophagosome formation and degradation, the LC3-II levels in the presence or absence of lysosomal inhibitors can be used as "autophagomometer" to measure the autophagic-flux [45]. Under steady-state conditions (unstarved), the treatment with chloroquine (CQ), a lysosomotropic agent that inhibits the lysosomal proteases, resulted in a comparable increase in the LC3-II level in Als2-/- cells with those in wild-type (Figure 8A), indicating that loss of ALS2 by itself does not seem to affect the formation of autophagosomes in cells. Further, a short-term starvation in wild-type and Als2-/- fibroblasts resulted in decreased levels of p62 and LC3-II, indicating an enhancement of autophagy-dependent protein degradation in both cell types (Figure 8A). Notably, under such starved conditions, the LC3-II levels in Als2-/- cells were significantly higher than those in wild-type cells (Figure 8A), suggesting that a degree of autophagic clearance was affected by ALS2 loss.
###end p 49
###begin title 50
Loss of ALS2 results in decreased levels of the lysosome-dependent degradation of LC3 in fibroblasts.
###end title 50
###begin p 51
###xml 1 2 1 2 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 112 116 112 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 116 119 116 119 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 128 131 128 131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 376 377 368 369 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 487 491 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 491 494 483 486 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 499 503 491 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 503 506 495 498 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 768 769 752 753 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 854 855 838 839 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 1070 1078 1044 1052 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">post hoc</italic>
###xml 1130 1131 1104 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1141 1142 1115 1116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1187 1191 1161 1165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1191 1194 1165 1168 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1197 1198 1171 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1207 1208 1181 1182 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</bold>
###xml 1341 1345 1315 1319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1345 1348 1319 1322 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1558 1562 1532 1536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Als2</italic>
###xml 1562 1565 1536 1539 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 132 136 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 507 511 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1349 1353 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) Effect of ALS2 expression on the autophagic flux in fibroblasts. Fibroblasts derived from either wild-type (Als2+/+) or Als2-/- mice were incubated in a starvation medium with or without 0.5 microM chloroquine (CQ) for 6 hr. Equal amount of protein from total lysates were analyzed by immunoblotting using antibodies as indicated. Alpha(alpha)-tubulin served as control. (B) Effect of ALS2 expression on the autophagic flux in fibroblasts.
